<div id="review_3570983925" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3570983925" />
    <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale"><img alt="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577855357p2/69106439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3570983925?book_show_action=true">Sep 28, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale">Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/41827561-radio-silence">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3570983925" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8012017088233026534"><i>”Hello. I hope somebody is listening.”</i> <br/><br/>I think by now this quote made its way into the most epic quotes of all time and I can totally understand all the hype this book got. When I joined goodreads back in 2017 “Radio Silence” was all over my feed and people were raving about it like crazy. I had no idea what all the fuss was about but three years later and countless books in between I finally get it. XD Alice Oseman’s book is amazing, epic, brilliant and most of all it’s relatable af! <br/><br/>As an auth</span>
  <span id="freeText8012017088233026534" style="display:none"><i>”Hello. I hope somebody is listening.”</i> <br /><br />I think by now this quote made its way into the most epic quotes of all time and I can totally understand all the hype this book got. When I joined goodreads back in 2017 “Radio Silence” was all over my feed and people were raving about it like crazy. I had no idea what all the fuss was about but three years later and countless books in between I finally get it. XD Alice Oseman’s book is amazing, epic, brilliant and most of all it’s relatable af! <br /><br />As an author it’s not easy to capture the voice of a generation but I think Oseman did it masterfully. Truth be told, it’s more than the voice of a generation, it’s the voice of many generations that all went through the same thing. Did I lose you already? What I’m trying to say is that this book is timeless because it speaks to every teenager and young adult that ever went through adolescence.<br /><br /><b>“Radio Silence”</b> tackles the strong bonds of friendships you only seem to have as a teen, it addresses the insecurities of young adults, the urgency and intensity of emotions, it shows that our educational system is far from perfect and that good grades aren’t everything in life, it makes room for individualism and it demonstrates that parents can influence their children in the best but also in the worst way possible. It plays with the idea of the internet as a medium that can connect people all over the world but it also illustrates how easy it is to hurt people and their privacy. <br /><br />Seriously, this book gives so many thought-provoking impulses it’s hard to write it all into a summary, which only seems to emphasise my earlier statement of Oseman’s skill to capture the voice of a generation. People are complex, relationships are complicated and the way to your true self is paved with plenty of seemingly insurmountable obstacles. So just another ordinary day in the life of a young adult, right? ;-P<br /><br />trigger warnings: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[emotional parental abuse, depression (implied), suicidal thoughts (heavily implied), online bullying, teens drinking alcohol <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>The characters:</b><br /><br /><u>
  <b>This is my spoilery spoiler section and if you haven’t already read the book: Well, pirates ye be warned! ;-P This said: Welcome to Universe City, I’m sure you’ll have a lovely time with Radio and his sidekicks!</b>
</u><br /><br /><b>Frances Janvier:</b><br /><br /><i>”Being clever was, after all, my primary source of self-esteem. I’m a very sad person, in all senses of the word, but at least I was going to get into university.”</i> <br /><br />I really liked Frances! I mean I was never as good at school as her but I kind of admire her for getting good grades while following her obsession with “Radio Silence”. It’s no small feat and I really appreciated the idea of a character that’s good at school but also has a very creative streak. =) For some reason this is pretty rare in books and I don’t know why. XD Also the distinction between “School Frances” and “Normal Frances “ was amazing and very relatable. As a teen a lot of us are insecure and act differently when they are around their friends so this was such a great way to represent that sentiment. Also now is the moment I have to mention that I want Aled’s and France’s wardrobe! *lol* Seriously, their clothes are amazing! &lt;3 I would have loved to get my hands on them. Haha! Anyway, back to Frances as a character! I loved her compassion and that she always tried to do the right thing and was very responsible. Plus she was a really great friend! I hope we’ll see more of her in other books but I’m not sure she’s going to be in one of the others?! Guess I’ll have to find out. <br /><br /><i>”I couldn’t quite believe how much I seriously loved Aled Last, even if it wasn’t in the ideal way that would make it socially acceptable for us to live together until we die.”</i><br /><br /><b>Aled Last:</b><br /><br /><i>”it’s honestly fine!!!! what’s up?<br />if you’re feeling crap it’s always better to talk about it</i><br /><br />I really wish Aled would have taken his own advice! I know he’s the silent, withdrawn and broody kind of type but a lot of his problems could have been tackled if he would have just talked about them. Then again his mother certainly didn’t make it easy to develop some self-esteem, let alone to talk about his problems. (I’m so angry at his mom btw!!!) I felt so, so sorry for him and I was glad Frances and Daniel were able to see the true Aled. My heart really bled for this boy and it made me so sad that his mother couldn’t see how beautiful he was! &lt;3 I mean he made a podcast thousands of people followed and listened to, they even made fanart of it and yet his mother had nothing better to do than to destroy every little piece of him. &gt;_&lt; It killed me. Really. Aled suffered so much and I wish I could have jumped right into the book and saved him! He didn’t want to go to university and he was drowning in despair, which got more and more apparent with every episode he made. Those last few episodes? It just hurt... because they were a reflection of his true life and helplessness. T_T<br /><br /><i>”Sometimes I think if nobody spoke to me, I’d never speak again.”</i> <br /><br /><i>”I can take a little beating now and then. I’m a tough one. I’m a star. I’m steel-chested and diamond-eyed. Cyborgs live and then they break, but I’ll never break. Even when my bone dust drifts over the City walls, I’ll be living and I’ll be flying, and I will wave and laugh.”</i><br /><br /><b>Daniel Jun:</b><br /><br /><i>”We were so important to each other. We’d tell each other everything and anything. We were each other’s first everything. First and only everything. He’s – he’s an angel.”</i><br /><br />Daniel might have appeared to be a study machine but deep down he was a really nice guy and it was pretty obvious that he cared about Aled. With his neat appearance and orderly life he’s the complete opposite of Aled, yet he still enjoyed being with his friend. Daniel was so focused on school that it wasn’t easy to see his true self but the longer I read the more I began to warm to him. XD Guess I made the same experience like Frances. ;-)<br /><br /><b>Carys:</b><br /><br /><i>Carol raised an eyebrow. “Well, it is how it is. I’m not here to see you and, frankly, I don’t want to. I want to talk to my real child.”<br />“I don’t think you deserve to,” said Carys, and I could feel the inaudible gasps of everyone in the room.</i><br /><br />Okay, I admit it: There was a moment when I wanted to punch Carys in the face! I mean if it would have been my brother suffering so much I would have run to him in a heartbeat. But then again she thought that she was the problem and that Aled would be fine. Thankfully Frances could persuade her to seek him out and the moment she realized her mother was destroying Aled she became the lioness I wanted her to be! XD I loved how she defended Aled and that she gave her mother a run for her money because quite honestly this was what I wanted her to do the entire book! I’m so glad Aled and her reconciled and I was glad Frances and Carys got a chance to talk about the night she vanished. <br /><br /><b>The relationships:</b><br /><br /><u>Frances &amp; Aled:</u><br /><br /><i>He laughed again and hid his face under the blanket.<br />“Why are you so nice to me?”<br />“Because I’m an angel.”<br />“You are.” He stretched out his arm and patted me on the head. “And I’m platonically in love with you.”<br />“That was literally the boy-girl version of ‘no homo’, but I appreciate the sentiment.”</i><br /><br />Boy their relationship was one hell of a rollercoaster! When they got to know each other and started to work on “Universe City” I was so happy for them but the more Aled’s mother and the fandom of Radio interfered, the more their friendship got under attack. I really would have loved for them just to do their own thing and not to be bothered by anything but of course life had other plans. I mean it’s no wonder Aled kind of broke under the pressure. Between the constant emotional abuse of his mother and the personal attacks of the fandom it would have been hard for anyone to keep on swimming. So bless Frances for always trying to reach out to him! Heaven knows Aled’s condition and his character didn’t make it easy to get through to him, but she never gave up on him and that’s what true friends do! Even though I’ve to admit that he said quite hurtful things to her and it’s no wonder she was insecure about their friendship. Still, at the end they found together again and I was very glad they did! =)<br /><br /><i>He wrenched his hand back. “It’s fine. She’s always like this.”<br />“Does she hurt you?” I said. “Tell me if she hurts you. Right now. I’m serious.”<br />“No. I swear she doesn’t. He waved his injured hand. “This was an accident.”<br />“That’s not right. She can’t just – She just – What the fuck, I mean ...”</i><br /><br /><i>”I’m just the replacement. You’re obsessed with me. Just the same as Carys, and you’ve managed to fuck up the only thing I had, the only good thing I fucking have, just like you managed to fuck up Carys’s. D’you fancy me as well?”</i><br /><br /><i>”Do you want to be famous?”<br />“I just ... want to be special.”<br />“You are special.”<br />He laughed and said, “Shut up.”</i><br /><br /><u>Frances &amp; her mum:</u><br /><br /><i>”Don’t let him escape!” said Mum. “This could be your only chance at securing a spouse!”</i> <br /><br />I swear Frances’s mum is kick-ass! I strive to be as cool as her once my little one is in her teens! I mean that woman wore a unicorn onesie and was basically an angel! I loved that Frances could talk with her about everything and that she always listened to her daughter’s troubles. She didn’t judge and let Frances figure out things for herself and most importantly: She accepted her the way she was!!! Even when Frances told her that she didn’t want to go to university she was totally okay with it and respected her daughter’s decision! I just loved that she was so supportive! She was the total opposite of Aled’s mum and I really liked that parents weren’t just mentioned as a footnote in “Radio Silence” but actually were a part of their children’s lives! =) This is really rare in YA and I appreciated it immensely! <br /><br /><i>”I don’t think I want to go to university.”<br />“Oh, Frances.” She didn’t sound disappointed. “That’s okay.”<br />“Is it okay?” I asked, because I wasn’t sure.<br />“Yes,” she said. “It’s okay.”</i><br /><br /><u>Aled &amp; his mum:</u><br /><br /><i>”She looked terrifying, in that classic white, middle-class mum sort of way. Dyed cropped hair, slightly round physique, a smile that said ‘Can I get you a cup of tea?’ and eyes that said ‘I will burn everything you love.’</i><br /><br />I really hated this woman! So, so much! GRRR!!! She stands for everything a parent shouldn’t do and be and URGH! I just couldn’t with her! I mean who ruins their children’s life? Who takes a scissor and cuts their son’s hair even though he said he doesn’t want to cut it?! Like seriously!?? And don’t even get me started on her changing Aled’s room! That was his personal space his safe haven and she destroyed it because she thought it was too messy?! WTF?! YOU. DON’T. INVADE. YOUR. CHILD’S. PRVIVATE. SPACE. EVER.!!! You let them put up posters, you let them scribble poetry on a white board, you idk give them room to breathe and to be who they are!! You don’t destroy their home! And then the thing with Aled’s dog Brian?! WTH?! Which mother does things like that?! I’m outraged and furious about this behaviour from a person that should lover her child unconditionally! The emotional abuse this woman put her children through isn’t normal and it’s extremely appalling! She might have never raised her hand against them but the emotional scars her actions left are at least as severe as if she would have hit them. All throughout the entire book I just wanted to call the youth welfare office! &gt;_&lt; I can’t with this woman. I just can’t! I’m so glad Carys and Aled aren’t with her anymore. They suffered enough! And this from a woman that birthed them and should have loved them... *shakes head*<br /><br /><i>”Aled was going to cry when he saw this.<br />She had taken his private space – his home – and destroyed it.<br />She took everything he loved and ruined it.”</i><br /><br /><i>”But we were sitting under the streetlamps and Aled was shaking in my arms and this was real, this was happening. She was taking everything Aled had and burning it. She was burning him, slowly, until he died.”</i> <br /><br /><u>Daniel &amp; Aled:</u><br /><br /><i>”I think we were so caught up in each other that we just... missed all the heteronormative propaganda that’s thrust at you when you’re that age.”</i><br /><br />Ahh those two were actually kinda cute! Daniel broke my heart when he spoke about their relationship with Frances though. I think for him it must have been very difficult to deal with Aled. On the one hand he was his best friend and knew him better than anyone else but on the other hand he had no idea how he truly felt about him. I could understand why Aled was insecure about outing himself as demisexual. A lot of people never heard of it and he had only just begun to figure out what this meant for him as a person. I’m sure he didn’t want to hurt Daniel and so he rather pushed him away instead of talking things out. Anyway. It made me happy that they eventually managed to speak about it and I hope that one day they’ll reach the moment when they’ll both feel comfortable enough to show the world. =) <br /><br /><i>”It was all just for us in private, like we had to protect it, because we didn’t want the rest of the world to ruin it. I don’t really know why... I guess it didn’t feel like we were in a relationship at all. Because we were best friends, first and foremost. So we never knew how we’d explain it to people.”</i><br /><br /><i>”I think everyone’s a bit bored with boy-girl romances anyway,” he said. “I think the world’s had enough of those, to be honest.”</i><br /><br /><b>The reps and diversity:</b><br /><br />This is an Alice Oseman book so the reps and the diversity were amazing! We have Frances who’s bisexual and English/Ethiopian; then there is Aled - the second MC - who is demisexual and his best friend/boyfriend Daniel who is South Korean and gay! Rain a friend of Frances is Indian and last but not least there’s Carys – Aled’s sister – who is a lesbian. So you just gotta love the diversity in this book! Also I think Aled is showing signs of depression but it’s never really verified. (though pretty much implied!) <br /><br /><b>Conclusion:</b><br /><br />This is probably the best contemporary book I ever read and considering it’s a genre I rarely dive into this should tell you enough! Alice Oseman is a genius and the characters she created, their struggles and friendships, their hopes and dreams, their fears and doubts; they all felt real and more than just a little relatable! <b>“Radio Silence”</b> is the accurate voice of numerous generations, describing the one thing every one of us has to experience in order to become who we truly are: Adolescence! ;-)</span>
  <a data-text-id="8012017088233026534" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a title="emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="emma" href="/user/show/32879029-emma">emma</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2117451269" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer8948261058854276158">Look at me posting it up!!! Find this review hereeeeee: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.com/2017/10/31/contemporary-reviews-because-reading-this-genre-always-goes-so-well-for-me/'>https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.co...</a><br/>---------<br/><br/>What. Is. This. Book.<br/><br/>Like...how do I review a book if I don’t know my feelings on it? AND HOW DO I DECIDE WHAT MY FEELINGS ARE IF I DON’T KNOW WHAT IT <i>IS</i>?<br/><br/>Okay. Let me go with the old classics and start off by stating what I know: a synopsis and the few concrete opinions I have.<br/><br/>So in this book we follow Frances, a studying machine who is a huge fangirl of a podcast (for a podcast? What is the </span>
  <span id="freeText8948261058854276158" style="display:none">Look at me posting it up!!! Find this review hereeeeee: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.com/2017/10/31/contemporary-reviews-because-reading-this-genre-always-goes-so-well-for-me/">https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.co...</a><br />---------<br /><br />What. Is. This. Book.<br /><br />Like...how do I review a book if I don’t know my feelings on it? AND HOW DO I DECIDE WHAT MY FEELINGS ARE IF I DON’T KNOW WHAT IT <i>IS</i>?<br /><br />Okay. Let me go with the old classics and start off by stating what I know: a synopsis and the few concrete opinions I have.<br /><br />So in this book we follow Frances, a studying machine who is a huge fangirl of a podcast (for a podcast? What is the proper grammar for “fangirl”). She then finds out that a total dweeb named Aled is the one making it, and they become friends and whatnot and are wildly successful and drama ensues or whatever. Aled has a lot of family drama. Things go down.<br /><br />That’s the story, morning glory.<br /><br />Now let’s get to the real treat: my opinions. How exciting.<br /><br />Most importantly, this book is SO EFFORTLESSLY DIVERSE. Frances is bisexual. Aled is asexual and gay. (This is technically something that is revealed later on in the story, but I don’t like treating sexuality like a spoiler generally. Ace representation especially is SO RARE and v important. So I’m not going to, like, hide that from you guys. It’s not even a huge reveal. It’s just character growth and recognition and whatnot.) Frances is also half-Ethiopian and has a single mother, as does Aled, I think. It’s all just very good. All YA should be as easily inclusive as this. It makes for a much richer story.<br /><br />Wow. How…<i>earnest</i>. Shiver.<br /><br />There’s also no romance in this book which is just...profoundly refreshing. But also kind of weird in this context? Because it seems <i>very</i> romancey at times. It just doesn’t end up that way. So I’d like more of this, please, but also less romancey even than this.<br /><br />The last good thing is that I read it in a day.<br /><br />FURTHERMORE.<br /><br />I did not really love or very much even like this book.<br /><br />I know. I don’t know how many reasons I have for it. This book and I just didn’t click. And even if there are things about it that are really very good, and even if generally I would recommend this book to those that are interested, I’m not going to make myself give this a rating that doesn’t feel true. <br /><br />I didn’t love the writing style. And overall I guess it just felt really strange to me. I felt so odd about marking this as “contemporary” because it DOESN’T FEEL LIKE THAT AT ALL. It’s so unrealistic as to almost not take place in our world. The way the characters act, but also just the way that people act as a whole...it felt like fantasy or magical realism. I don’t know. The plot jumped around a lot which, you know, didn’t exactly help to GROUND me in the magical world of steampunk whimsy in which we find ourselves.<br /><br />Plus reading about England is always slightly weird. It’s like America, but not! (Insert a million angry British people in the comments.)<br /><br />And “Universe City,” the podcast Aled makes/Frances obsesses over, is really just a copy of Welcome to Night Vale. It says it’s inspired by, but it’s really the same thing. And Welcome to Night Vale is a lot cooler and more exciting and interesting. <br /><br />This is so weird and choppy but I’m still REALLY TRYING TO FIGURE OUT WHY I DIDN’T LIKE THIS. I’M SORRY.<br /><br />Okay. I took a two week break to reflect. I vacationed, I sat on beaches, I looked out train windows onto rainy landscapes with my head resting on my hand, other tropes about thinking. And I think I know what it is.<br /><br />It’s...the characters.<br /><br />There’s a lot of insta-friendship, which always feels uncomfy. And everyone treats each other sh*ttily (I love making the word sh*t into an adverb) and do things that people would just like, never do. Everyone is flat, and if they’re not flat then they end up acting totally unrealistically and then that MAKES them flat and I don’t get it!!!!! I am so screaming into the void right now and even the void is like you’re not making any sense!!!!!!<br /><br />This is the worst review I’ve ever written. AND STILL I DON’T LIKE THIS BOOK.<br /><br />Bottom line: Yeah read this if you want to. Literally don’t listen to me at all. I’M DELETING MY ACCOUNT BYE</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6701246891581025075">This book missed the mark for me, but also helped me solidify the fact that I don't think I enjoy fandom books anymore. This book focuses a lot on a fictional podcast and fanart and fandom, and I just found it more cringy than relatable. I liked Aled, so I wish this book was about him rather than Frances. I just couldn't relate at all to the storyline, and the overarching conflict of the characters not wanting to go to college ended up being so flat with such an easy solution--then don't? <br/><br/>I'm su</span>
  <span id="freeText6701246891581025075" style="display:none">This book missed the mark for me, but also helped me solidify the fact that I don't think I enjoy fandom books anymore. This book focuses a lot on a fictional podcast and fanart and fandom, and I just found it more cringy than relatable. I liked Aled, so I wish this book was about him rather than Frances. I just couldn't relate at all to the storyline, and the overarching conflict of the characters not wanting to go to college ended up being so flat with such an easy solution--then don't? <br /><br />I'm sure other people who see themselves in this book would love it a whole lot more than I did, but even though it was an easy read that I flew through, I just wasn't wowed. I don't anticipate I'll read anything else from Alice Oseman other than her graphic novel series.</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5138611-cece-problemsofabooknerd?shelf=lgbtqia">lgbtqia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5138611-cece-problemsofabooknerd?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5138611-cece-problemsofabooknerd?shelf=female-protag">female-protag</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5138611-cece-problemsofabooknerd?shelf=my-books">my-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1797773206" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10772202879716192442">*4.5/5<br/><br/>I honestly can’t tell you how long it’s been since I stayed up too late, not even realizing what time it was because I was so desperate to finish a story. Brilliant. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1643663493" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1643663493" />
    <a title="Nat" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23381142-nat"><img alt="Nat" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588309995p2/23381142.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1643663493?book_show_action=true">May 20, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nat" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nat" href="/user/show/23381142-nat">Nat</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23381142-nat?shelf=diverse-reads">diverse-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1643663493" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer565467225002390678"><i>“Hello. I hope somebody is listening.”</i><br/><br/><b>Radio Silence</b> has been on my wishlist for ages, so I figured the time has come to pick it up. And wow was time right.<br/><br/>We follow Frances Janvier's final school year. Frances has always been a study machine with one goal, elite university. Nothing will stand in her way; not friends, not a guilty secret – not even the person she is on the inside.<br/><br/>Frances is obsessed with Universe City, a YouTube podcast show about a suit-wearing student detective looking for a wa</span>
  <span id="freeText565467225002390678" style="display:none"><i>“Hello. I hope somebody is listening.”</i><br><br><b>Radio Silence</b> has been on my wishlist for ages, so I figured the time has come to pick it up. And wow was time right.<br><br>We follow Frances Janvier's final school year. Frances has always been a study machine with one goal, elite university. Nothing will stand in her way; not friends, not a guilty secret – not even the person she is on the inside.<br><br>Frances is obsessed with Universe City, a YouTube podcast show about a suit-wearing student detective looking for a way to escape a sci-fi, monster-infested university.<br><br><i>“Nobody knew who made the podcast, but it was the voice of the narrator that got me addicted to the show – it has a kind of softness. It makes you want to fall asleep. In the least weird way possible, it’s a bit like someone stroking your hair.”</i><br><br>That's what I thought when I listened to my first podcast episode: it makes you want to fall asleep (in the best way possible).<br><br>Oh, and Frances is also mixed-race &amp; bisexual.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1471155886ra/20006415.gif" width="246" height="246" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>This review contains <b>mild *spoilers*</b>.<br><br>When Frances meets Aled Last, the shy genius behind her favourite podcast, she discovers a new freedom.<br><br><i>“I never told anyone about Universe City,” he said, glancing back at me. “I thought they’d think I was weird.”<br>There were a hundred things I could have said in reply to that, but I just said:<br>“Same.”</i><br><br>Same here, too.<br><br>I also loved how they slowly became good friends, it's one of my favorite things to read about in books:<br><br><i>“Just before he left, as we were standing in the doorway, I said:<br>“Where did you get your shoes? They’re so nice.”<br>He looked at me like I’d told him he’d won the lottery.<br>“ASOS,” he said.<br>“Ah, cool.”<br>“They’re …” He almost didn’t say it. “I know they’re weird. They were in the women’s section.”<br>“Oh. They don’t look like women’s shoes.” I looked at his feet. “They don’t look like men’s shoes either. They’re just shoes.” I looked back at him and smiled, not quite sure where I was going with this. He was staring at me, his expression now completely unreadable.<br>“I have a coat from Topman,” I continued. “And I tell you what, the men’s section of Primark is the best for Christmas jumpers.”</i><br><br>Yes! Thank you for addressing this in writing.<br><br>And for a second there I was troubled that this was going to become a love story, but I needn't have worried.<br><br><i>“I just sort of want to say something before we continue.<br>You probably think that Aled Last and I are going to fall in love or something. Since he is a boy and I am a girl.<br>I just wanted to say –<br>We don’t.<br>That’s all.”</i><br><br>I felt so surprised (in a good way) when she addressed the reader. I even had that Robert De Niro moment:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1471155886ra/20006416.gif" width="400" height="236" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But I just... I <b>loved</b> how well-developed and real the friendship between Frances and Aled was:<br><br><i>“Our friendship had become this:<br><br>(00:00) Frances Janvier<br>HAPPY BIRTHDAY HOPE YOU’RE FEELING PARTY AF<br>LOVE U LOADS U BEAUTIFUL MAN<br>CAN’T BELIEVE MY SMALL BUDDY IS A MAN NOW<br>I’M CRYING<br><br>(00:02) Aled Last<br>why are you tormenting me with cringe messages like this<br><br>(00:03) Frances Janvier<br>¯\_(ツ)_/¯<br><br>(00: 03) Aled Last<br>Wow<br>thank u tho luv u (✿♥‿♥)<br><br>(00:04) Frances Janvier”<br>THAT was cringe m8<br><br>(00:04) Aled Last<br>that was payback "</i><br><br>Literally cry-laughing over their messages.<br><br>Speaking of... the humor in this book was right up my alley.<br><br><i>“There was a huge Facebook event for the post-exams night happening at Johnny R’s on the same day, which everyone in sixth form had been invited to, but I didn’t really want to go. Firstly, everyone was just gonna get drunk, which I could do perfectly well by myself in my lounge while watching YouTube videos instead of having to worry about catching the last train home or avoiding sexual assault. Secondly, I hadn’t really spoken to any of my school friends apart from Raine very recently, and I think if we were in The Sims, our friendship bar would almost be back to nothing.”</i><br><br>I don't know why, but that Sims reference made me crack up for days.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1471155886ra/20006417.gif" width="325" height="246" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>...On a more serious note, I went into this book thinking that Frances was asexual (not bisexual), so that was a mistake on my part. But <b>Radio Silence</b> talked about really important topics in such an inclusive way, I loved it.<br><br><i>“Like, it’s one of the reasons that I got so into Universe City in the first place. Because Radio falls in love with all sorts of people, boys and girls and other genders and … like, aliens and stuff.” I laughed and he smiled too.<br>“I think everyone’s a bit bored with boy-girl romances anyway,” he said. “I think the world’s had enough of those, to be honest.”</i><br><br>True!!!<br><br>Also, the pop-culture references were written in such a smooth way!! There was talk of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1545866000" rel="nofollow noopener">Harry Potter</a>, Youtubers, <a href="https://twitter.com/bookspoils" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> (including tweets)... and again, the instant messages between Frances and Aled were hysterical.<br><br>Social media was just handled in a really well way, both the positive and the negative aspects. I mean, when some people in the fandom were acting like literal detectives trying to expose someone online, it was scary. Not gonna lie.<br>Messing with the privacy of a person who clearly wanted to remain anonymous? Not cool.<br><br><i>“It was disgusting. People who knew Aled in real life had taken stuff from his private Facebook. They’d listened in on my conversation with Jess and quoted me. What was this? Who did they think I was? A celebrity?”</i><br><br>I'm very glad Alice Oseman included this.<br><br>Also, on a completely unrelated note— can we take a minute to appreciate Raine? Because I loved it whenever she showed up. She just said whatever she wanted whenever she wanted. Incredible.<br><br><i>“Is that an ‘Oh my God you look absolutely ridiculous’?” I said, getting into the passenger seat, “because that’s an understandable reaction.”<br>“No, I mean I didn’t know you were so … pop punk. I thought I was gonna have to corrupt the nerdy one, but … you’re not actually a nerd, are you?”<br>She appeared to be being genuine.<br>“This is real, this is me,” I said.<br>She blinked. “Did you just quote Camp Rock at me? That’s not very pop punk.”<br>“I’ve gotta go my own way.”<br>“Okay, firstly, that’s High School Musical …”</i><br><br>Ha! She took my line about Camp Rock!!<br>Also, quoting old Disney Channel movies in books? Yes, please.<br><br>Truly though, Lorraine Sengupta had my heart because her lines were the absolute best. She's a sunshine angel.<br><br>Oh, and as I mentioned before about asexuality... I was really glad that it did end up being included when Aled mentioned that he's demisexual!<br><br>I pretty much adored everything about <b>Radio Silence</b>, and my only tiny (really tiny) complaint being that the word 'literally' was used one too many times for my liking. I enjoy using it too, but while reading I prefer seeing it in moderation.<br><br>Also, I just wanted to mention that this book had so many great recommendations for music artists (London Grammar, Nero, Madeon...). And yet I still somehow ended up listening to <a href="https://soundcloud.com/chaz-youngren/that-would-be-enough" rel="nofollow noopener">this next song</a> on repeat because I'm obsessed with Phillipa Soo's voice. <br>(Every single time she sings “<i>I wrote to the General a month ago</i>,” a piece of my heart cracks.)<br><br><i>*Note: I'm an Amazon Affiliate. If you're interested in buying</i> <b>Radio Silence</b>, <i>just click on the image below to go through my link. I'll make a small commission!*</i><br><a target="_blank" href="https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0007559240/ref=as_li_tl?ie=UTF8&amp;camp=1789&amp;creative=9325&amp;creativeASIN=0007559240&amp;linkCode=as2&amp;tag=natalie013-20&amp;linkId=73ffff6e164180b80ad4b819d980a0c7" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1482928505i/21562288.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1482928505i/21562289.gif" width="1" height="1" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a href="https://bookspoils.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">This review and more can be found on my blog.</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="565467225002390678" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <a title="Kai" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41788524-kai"><img alt="Kai" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573562141p2/41788524.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1249716947?book_show_action=true">Apr 08, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kai" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kai" href="/user/show/41788524-kai">Kai</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007559244" href="/book/show/40119231-radio-silence">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=queer">queer</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=2016">2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1249716947" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4861224841391515259"><i>"Everything's better under the stars, I suppose. If we get another life after we die, I'll meet you there."</i><br/><br/>4.5/5 stars<br/><br/>A girl pretending to be someone else entirely. A boy who can peel away her layers. A friendship so deep they'll never want to lose each other. And secrets that could destroy it all.<br/><br/>I've you've read <i>Solitaire</i> or <i>Radio Silence</i> you'll know that she's one of us. Movie and book nerd, internet and 90's kid, passionate procrastinator, feminist, possibly awkward. Which is the main reason</span>
  <span id="freeText4861224841391515259" style="display:none"><i>"Everything's better under the stars, I suppose. If we get another life after we die, I'll meet you there."</i><br /><br />4.5/5 stars<br /><br />A girl pretending to be someone else entirely. A boy who can peel away her layers. A friendship so deep they'll never want to lose each other. And secrets that could destroy it all.<br /><br />I've you've read <i>Solitaire</i> or <i>Radio Silence</i> you'll know that she's one of us. Movie and book nerd, internet and 90's kid, passionate procrastinator, feminist, possibly awkward. Which is the main reason her writing is so close to my heart. It's highly relatable and highly sarcastic. No wonder I read this in a day. This was even better than her debut novel.<br /><br />There's many more reasons this book made happy:<br />•I just love the characters, especially Frances' mom. She's the best. And even though you won't like the evil Mom-next-door, she's someone you'll recognise from your non-book life.<br />•Thumbs up also for talking feminism, diversity, and sexual identity.<br />•CAMEOS. I NEED MORE NICK&amp;CHARLIE IN MY LIFE PRETTY PLEASE.<br /><br />The only thing I can criticise - and where I had to take away half a star - is the clichéd drama. But that shall be forgiven. 99% of books have that moment where you roll your eyes because of some big misunderstanding, where you know that if they'd just talk, it could be sorted out in a minute.<br /><br />Now, how long will I have to wait for a new Oseman book?<br /><br /><br /><a href="https://www.instagram.com/fantasticbooksandwheretofindem/" rel="nofollow noopener">Find more of my books on Instagram</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="4861224841391515259" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2504847665" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2504847665" />
    <a title="chan ☆" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48727754-chan"><img alt="chan ☆" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596680961p2/48727754.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2504847665?book_show_action=true">Aug 25, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="chan ☆" class="user" itemprop="url" name="chan ☆" href="/user/show/48727754-chan">chan ☆</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48727754-chan?shelf=ya-contemporary">ya-contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48727754-chan?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48727754-chan?shelf=2018">2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2504847665" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16772950724566374562"><b>"if you like it, then it <i>is</i> brilliant."</b><br/><br/>shit y'all. i'm honestly at a loss for words when it comes to this book. as with many books, i was influenced by another person to read this one. specifically by kat of paperbackdreams on youtube. if you watch her, you'll understand the expectations that i had going into this.<br/><br/>it wasn't at all what i expected. i didn't know much about the plot going in, purposefully. but i didn't expect a book about a girl in her senior year of high school & a boy with an an</span>
  <span id="freeText16772950724566374562" style="display:none"><b>"if you like it, then it <i>is</i> brilliant."</b><br /><br />shit y'all. i'm honestly at a loss for words when it comes to this book. as with many books, i was influenced by another person to read this one. specifically by kat of paperbackdreams on youtube. if you watch her, you'll understand the expectations that i had going into this.<br /><br />it wasn't at all what i expected. i didn't know much about the plot going in, purposefully. but i didn't expect a book about a girl in her senior year of high school &amp; a boy with an anonymous youtube channel to be so stark and poignant. <br /><br />there was a lot to love. the format of the book, despite the (sorry) lack of plot lent itself well to binge reading. every chapter ended with SUCH. QUOTABLE. LINES. the idea that just because something is "typical" it doesn't have to be the right choice for you. the characters felt real, lovely, and so so imperfect. and the relationships were impeccably nuanced. all things that i need in books.<br /><br />PLUS! the boy/girl friendship and <b>NOT BANGIN</b> rep was fantastic.<br /><br /><b>the only reason i couldn't 5 star this is because i'm old.</b> truly. there was just a certain level of disconnect from the characters' struggles given that i'm already out of university and in the real world. i felt myself remembering some of that "what am i going to do with my life" angst that i had back then but it's hard to truly relate 5 years later. <br /><br />but that's not a bad thing. books are not written solely for me to relate to. and i <b>still</b> felt the beautiful sentiment that this book had to offer. go read this, especially if you're in high school. you'll find yourself wishing frances &amp; aled were your friends too.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16772950724566374562" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3071125569?book_show_action=true">Dec 04, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Reading_ Tam_ Ishly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Reading_ Tam_ Ishly" href="/user/show/102159719-reading-tam-ishly">Reading_ Tam_ Ishly</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3071125569" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14685993487222768868">This book is just so damn important! <br/><br/>One of the best coming of age, young adult books ever.<br/><br/>It's just so real.<br/><br/><br/>I started reading this one with no expectations. Good or bad, I was not going to care. I just jad to read it. The book has been slowly getting its audience ever since it got published.<br/><br/>This book is just not about the dilemma of the young who are getting into University and handling social media. This book is more than that. It talks about passion, the difficult situations the younger gener</span>
  <span id="freeText14685993487222768868" style="display:none">This book is just so damn important! <br /><br />One of the best coming of age, young adult books ever.<br /><br />It's just so real.<br /><br /><br />I started reading this one with no expectations. Good or bad, I was not going to care. I just jad to read it. The book has been slowly getting its audience ever since it got published.<br /><br />This book is just not about the dilemma of the young who are getting into University and handling social media. This book is more than that. It talks about passion, the difficult situations the younger generation has to face where the so called adults decide everything for them thinking they are making their lives easier (which I would say, they don't most of the time but rather end up hurting them more and make them more confused!).<br /><br />The book wastes no words. The book gives importance to every character involved. The writing style is simple and maintains an uninterrupted flow till the end. The character representation is diverse and perfect. The character development is so wholesome and the chemistry so relevantly realistically strong. The plot is direct and consuming. The ending is simply satisfying. Everything from the beginning was set up well and the whole book answers everything in itself. <br /><br />I have got one most hateful parent character (Aled's mother) and one of the most strong, lovely single parent character (Frances' mom). <br />Various important themes regarding lgbt, mental health, academic choices, physical and emotional abuse, friendship, social anxiety issues, how social media affects the ones who are handling them have been represented so well. The emotions are out there staring right at you and you just cannot escape them. <br /><br />I feel so good having read this book. My reading soul just found one of its missing pieces!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14685993487222768868" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_43884209'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/43884209-get-a-life-chloe-brown"><img alt="Get a Life, Chloe Brown (The Brown Sisters, #1)" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1553318108l/43884209._SX98_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('84OjGHJZ97EDQDFyoB5ocd53TGRb818y2cicOiXxDEzQAp38jNYeRDXmnUqSRdwBGirzrqQpzmSKNDxEXXKmcA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('wS1IyFS7IntNdFGNLhsITCysYOmFz/meWac3f87RrFPirHYsqjTLjnvS/bUcQLw86PHfI3oVaMgKW5cBtlIGbw==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/7789423.Alice_Oseman">About Alice Oseman</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/7789423.Alice_Oseman"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1603122242p3/7789423.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/7789423.Alice_Oseman">Alice Oseman

12,517
followers

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer18055682104951254518">Alice Oseman is an author/illustrator and was born in 1994 in Kent, England. She has written four YA contemporary novels about teenage disasters: SOLITAIRE, RADIO SILENCE, I WAS BORN FOR THIS, and LOVELESS. She is also the creator of LGBTQ+ YA romance webcomic HEARTSTOPPER, which is now published in physical form by Hachette Children's Books.<br/><br/>Alice’s first novel SOLITAIRE was published when she was</span>
  <span id="freeText18055682104951254518" style="display:none">Alice Oseman is an author/illustrator and was born in 1994 in Kent, England. She has written four YA contemporary novels about teenage disasters: SOLITAIRE, RADIO SILENCE, I WAS BORN FOR THIS, and LOVELESS. She is also the creator of LGBTQ+ YA romance webcomic HEARTSTOPPER, which is now published in physical form by Hachette Children's Books.<br /><br />Alice’s first novel SOLITAIRE was published when she was nineteen. Her YA novels have been nominated for the YA Book Prize, the Inky Awards, and the Goodreads Choice Award, and HEARTSTOPPER has been optioned for TV. She can usually be found staring aimlessly at computer screens, questioning the meaninglessness of existence, or doing anything and everything to avoid getting an office job.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18055682104951254518" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
